iMac Pro is being discontinued"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Chalk this up to inevitability. The iMac Pro is soon to be no more. First noted <a href=\"https:\/\/9to5mac.com\/2021\/03\/06\/apple-discontinues-imac-pro-apple-store-says-buy-while-supplies-last\/\">by 9to5Mac<\/a>, TechCrunch has since confirmed with Apple that the company will stop selling the all-in-one once the current stock is depleted.<\/p>\n<p>One configuration of the desktop is still available through Apple\u2019s site, listed as \u201cWhile Supplies Last\u201d and priced at $5,000. Some other versions can also still be found from third-party retailers, as well, if you&#8217;re so inclined.<\/p>\n<p>The space gray version of the popular system was initially introduced in 2017, ahead of the company\u2019s long-awaited revamp<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/04\/05\/apples-2019-imac-pro-will-be-shaped-by-workflows\/\"> of the Mac Pro<\/a>. Matthew called it a \u201clove letter to developers\u201d at the time, though that particular letter seems to have run its course.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"7QFjbIreml\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/06\/apple-27-inch-imac-review\/\">Apple 27-inch iMac review<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Apple 27-inch iMac review&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/06\/apple-27-inch-imac-review\/embed\/#?secret=7QFjbIreml\" data-secret=\"7QFjbIreml\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Since then, Apple has revamped the standard iMac, focusing the 27-inch model at those same users. The company notes that the model is currently the most popular iMac among professional users. The system has essentially made the Pro mostly redundant, prefiguring its sunsetting. Of course, there\u2019s also the new Mac Pro at the high end of Apple&#8217;s offerings.<\/p>\n<p>And let us not forget that the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/17\/macbook-air-m1-review-the-right-apple-silicon-mac-for-most\/\">Apple silicon-powered<\/a> iMacs should be on the way, as well. Thus far the company has revamped the MacBook, MacBook Air and Mac Mini with its proprietary chips. New versions of the 21.5-inch and 27-inch desktop are rumored for arrival later this year, sporting a long-awaited redesign to boot.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"GlesVlYH9z\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/12\/14\/apples-imac-pro-is-a-love-letter-to-developers\/\">Apple\u2019s iMac Pro is a love letter to developers<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Apple\u2019s iMac Pro is a love letter to developers&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/12\/14\/apples-imac-pro-is-a-love-letter-to-developers\/embed\/#?secret=GlesVlYH9z\" data-secret=\"GlesVlYH9z\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Chalk this up to inevitability. pro","slug":"imac-pro","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576594941"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576594941"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576594941"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576594941"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576594941"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2121927,"date":"2021-03-06T13:00:24","date_gmt":"2021-03-06T21:00:24","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2121927"},"modified":"2021-03-05T15:01:52","modified_gmt":"2021-03-05T23:01:52","slug":"investors-still-love-software-more-than-life","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/06\/investors-still-love-software-more-than-life\/","title":{"rendered":"Investors still love software more than life"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><em>Welcome back to The TechCrunch Exchange, a weekly startups-and-markets newsletter. It\u2019s broadly based on\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/the-exchange\/\">the daily column that appears on Extra Crunch<\/a>, but free, and made for your weekend reading. Want it in your inbox every Saturday morning? Sign up\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\">here<\/a>.<\/em><\/p>\n<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><em>Ready? Let\u2019s talk money, startups and spicy IPO rumors.<\/em><\/p>\n<p>Despite some <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/the-technology-selloff-is-getting-to-be-somewhat-material\/\">recent market volatility<\/a>, the valuations that software companies have generally been able to command in recent quarters have been impressive. On Friday, we <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/understanding-how-investors-value-growth-in-2021\/\">took a look<\/a> into why that was the case, and where the valuations could be a bit more bubbly than others. Per <a href=\"https:\/\/www.scribd.com\/document\/497410287\/Battery-Ventures-Software-2021-Report\">a report<\/a> written by few Battery Ventures investors, it stands to reason that the middle of the SaaS market could be where valuation inflation is at its peak.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Something to keep in mind if your startup\u2019s growth rate is ticking lower. But today, instead of being an enormous bummer and making you worry, I have come with some historically notable data to show you how good modern software startups and their larger brethren have it today.<\/p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-2121929 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-1.15.20-PM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"889\" height=\"204\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-1.15.20-PM.png 889w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-1.15.20-PM.png?resize=150,34 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-1.15.20-PM.png?resize=300,69 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-1.15.20-PM.png?resize=768,176 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-1.15.20-PM.png?resize=680,156 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-1.15.20-PM.png?resize=50,11 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 889px) 100vw, 889px\" \/><\/p>\n<p>In case you are not 100% infatuated with tables, let me save you some time. In the upper right we can see that SaaS companies today that are growing at less than 10% yearly are trading for an average of 6.9x their next 12 months\u2019 revenue.<\/p>\n<p>Back in 2011, SaaS companies that were growing at 40% or more were trading at 6.0x their next 12 month\u2019s revenue. Climate change, but for software valuations.<\/p>\n<p>One more note from my chat with Battery. Its investor Brandon Gleklen riffed with The Exchange on the definition of ARR and its nuances in the modern market. As more SaaS companies swap traditional software-as-a-service pricing for its consumption-based equivalent, he declined to quibble on definitions of ARR, instead arguing that all that matters in software revenues is whether they are being retained and growing over the long term. This brings us to our next topic.<\/p>\n<h2>Consumption v. SaaS pricing<\/h2>\n<p>I\u2019ve taken a number of earnings calls in the last few weeks with public software companies. One theme that\u2019s come up time and again has been consumption pricing versus more traditional SaaS pricing. There is some data showing that consumption-priced software companies are <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/18\/why-do-saas-companies-with-usage-based-pricing-grow-faster\/\">trading at higher multiples<\/a> than traditionally priced software companies, thanks to better-than-average retention numbers.<\/p>\n<p>But there is more to the story than just that. Chatting with Fastly CEO <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/joshuabixby?lang=en\">Joshua Bixby<\/a> after his company&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/investors.fastly.com\/files\/doc_financials\/2020\/q4\/4Q20-Shareholder-Letter.pdf\">earnings report<\/a>, we picked up an interesting and important market distinction between where consumption may be more attractive and where it may not be. Per Bixby, Fastly is seeing larger customers prefer consumption-based pricing because they can afford variability and prefer to have their bills tied more closely to revenue. Smaller customers, however, Bixby said, prefer SaaS billing because it has rock-solid predictability.<\/p>\n<p>I brought the argument to <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/poyark?lang=en\">Open View Partners Kyle Poyar<\/a>, a venture denizen who has been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/29\/subscription-based-pricing-is-dead-smart-saas-companies-are-shifting-to-usage-based-models\/\">writing on this topic for TechCrunch<\/a> in recent weeks. He noted that in some cases the opposite can be true, that variably priced offerings can appeal to smaller companies because their developers can often test the product without making a large commitment.<\/p>\n<p>So, perhaps we\u2019re seeing the software market favoring SaaS pricing among smaller customers when they are certain of their need, and choosing consumption pricing when they want to experiment first. And larger companies, when their spend is tied to equivalent revenue changes, bias toward consumption pricing as well.<\/p>\n<p>Evolution in SaaS pricing will be slow, and never complete. But folks really are thinking about it. Appian CEO <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/mattcalkins\/\">Matt Calkins<\/a> has a general pricing thesis that price should \u201chover\u201d under value delivered. Asked about the consumption-versus-SaaS topic, he was a bit coy, but did note that he was not \u201centirely happy\u201d with how pricing is executed today. He wants pricing that is a \u201cbetter proxy for customer value,\u201d though he declined to share much more.<\/p>\n<p>If you aren\u2019t thinking about this conversation and you run a startup, what&#8217;s up with that? More to come on this topic, including notes from an interview with the CEO of BigCommerce, who is betting on SaaS over the more consumption-driven Shopify.<\/p>\n<h2>Next Insurance, and its changing market<\/h2>\n<p>Next Insurance <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nextinsurance.com\/blog\/next-insurance-acquisition-ap-intego\/\">bought<\/a> another company this week. This time it was AP Intego, which will bring integration into various payroll providers for the digital-first SMB insurance provider. Next Insurance should be familiar because TechCrunch has <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/10\/as-next-insurance-makes-its-first-acquisition-insurtech-looks-energetic\/\">written about its growth a few times<\/a>. The company doubled its premium run rate to $200 million in 2020, for example.<\/p>\n<p>The AP Intego deal brings $185.1 million of active premium to Next Insurance, which means that the neo-insurance provider has grown sharply thus far in 2021, even without counting its organic expansion. But while the Next Insurance deal and the <a href=\"https:\/\/hippo-static.s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com\/investors\/Hippo+Reinvent+Presentation+March+2021+(vF+Announced).pdf\">impending Hippo SPAC<\/a> are neat notes from a hot private sector, insurtech has shed some of its public-market heat.<\/p>\n<p>Stocks of public neo-insurance companies like Root, Lemonade and MetroMile have <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/the-technology-selloff-is-getting-to-be-somewhat-material\/\">lost quite a lot of value in recent weeks<\/a>. So, the exit landscape for companies like Next and Hippo &#8212; yet-private insurtech startups with lots of capital backing their rapid premium growth &#8212; is changing for the worse.<\/p>\n<p>Hippo decided it will debut via a SPAC. But I doubt that Next Insurance will pursue a rapid ramp to the public markets until things smooth out. Not that it needs to go public quickly; it raised a quarter billion back in September of last year.<\/p>\n<h2>Various and Sundry<\/h2>\n<p>What else? Sisense, a <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/02\/kicking-off-2020-with-4-new-members-of-the-100m-arr-club\/\">$100 million ARR club<\/a> member, <a href=\"https:\/\/itbrief.com.au\/story\/sisense-appoints-new-cfo-adam-towns\">hired a new CFO<\/a>. So we expect them to go public inside the next four or five quarters.<\/p>\n<p>And the following chart, which is <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/deenashakir\/status\/1367243151769968642\">via Deena Shakir of Lux Capital<\/a>, via <a href=\"http:\/\/nasdaq.com\">Nasdaq<\/a>, via <a href=\"https:\/\/spacalpha.com\/\">SPAC Alpha<\/a>:<\/p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"aligncenter wp-image-2121931 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-2.00.13-PM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"551\" height=\"387\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-2.00.13-PM.png 551w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-2.00.13-PM.png?resize=150,105 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-2.00.13-PM.png?resize=300,211 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/Screen-Shot-2021-03-05-at-2.00.13-PM.png?resize=50,35 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 551px) 100vw, 551px\" \/><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"http:\/\/twitter.com\/alex\">Alex<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&nbsp;<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Welcome back to The TechCrunch Exchange, a weekly startups-and-markets newsletter. Exchange","slug":"the-exchange","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576765839"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576765839"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576765839"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576765839"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576765839"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2121859,"date":"2021-03-06T11:00:32","date_gmt":"2021-03-06T19:00:32","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2121859"},"modified":"2021-03-05T19:25:48","modified_gmt":"2021-03-06T03:25:48","slug":"the-product-manager-asterisk","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/06\/the-product-manager-asterisk\/","title":{"rendered":"The Product Manager asterisk"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Product manager might be one of the most grey roles within a startup. However, as a company progresses and the team grows, there comes a time when a founder needs to carve out dedicated roles. Of these positions, product management might be one of the most elusive \u2014 and key \u2014 roles to fill.<\/p>\n<p>Ken Norton, who recently left his job as director of product at Figma to consult rising PMs, thinks it\u2019s easier to start with defining what they aren\u2019t: the CEO of the product.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cProduct managers need to realize that there is a lot of janitorial work that gets done in product management,\u201d he said. \u201cIt\u2019s not fun or glamorous, and it\u2019s certainly not being the CEO of the product. It\u2019s just stuff that needs to get done.\u201d I wrote up a guide <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/product-manager-hiring-for-startups\/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">on how and when to hire your first product manager<\/a>\u00a0that expands on some of these insights, including how focus might be the biggest trait to interview for:<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/product-manager-hiring-for-startups\/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">How and when to hire your first product manager <\/a><\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/in-freemium-marketing-product-analytics-are-the-difference-between-conversion-and-confusion\/\">In freemium marketing, product analytics are the difference between conversion and confusion <\/a><\/li>\n<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/create-a-handbook-and-integrate-ai-to-onboard-remote-employees\/\">Create a handbook and integrate AI to onboard remote employees<\/a><\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<p>Hiring continues to be one of the hardest parts of building a startup, and those early employees can define the trajectory, culture and eventual success of it. Even during TC Sessions: Justice this past week, Precursor\u2019s Sydney Thomas explained how startups need to make \u201cpretty final decisions, pretty early on in what type of company you want to build.\u201d<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"L5Bg8dTFfm\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/product-manager-hiring-for-startups\/\">How and when to hire your first product manager<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;How and when to hire your first product manager&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/product-manager-hiring-for-startups\/embed\/#?secret=L5Bg8dTFfm\" data-secret=\"L5Bg8dTFfm\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>It\u2019s a slight asterisk to the common narrative of how startups pivot every other day. It\u2019s not that simple, and I\u2019ll probably remind you of that every other week, dear Startups Weekly readers.<\/p>\n<p>The rest of today\u2019s newsletter will include notes on a hot up-and-coming edtech IPO, an exit that includes Jay-Z, and the latest in agricultural tech robots. Also, remember you can always find me on Twitter @nmasc_ or e-mail me at <a href=\"mailto:natasha.m@techcrunch.com\">natasha.m@techcrunch.com<\/a>.<\/p>\n<h2><strong>The public markets get educated<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>It\u2019s been yet another busy week for the public markets. The startup tried to pain a picture of a path of profitability, with rising revenues as well as rising net losses. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/a-first-look-at-courseras-s-1-filing\/\">We get into the meat of it here.\u00a0<\/a><\/p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\" Weekly","slug":"startups-weekly","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576603287"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576603287"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576603287"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576603287"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576603287"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2121554,"date":"2021-03-06T08:08:51","date_gmt":"2021-03-06T16:08:51","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2121554"},"modified":"2021-03-06T08:21:32","modified_gmt":"2021-03-06T16:21:32","slug":"this-week-in-apps-app-store-bill-passes-az-house-deep-nostalgia-goes-viral-twitter-spaces-arrives-on-android","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/06\/this-week-in-apps-app-store-bill-passes-az-house-deep-nostalgia-goes-viral-twitter-spaces-arrives-on-android\/","title":{"rendered":"This Week in Apps: App Store bill passes AZ House, &#8216;deep nostalgia&#8217; goes viral, Twitter Spaces arrives on Android"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Welcome back to This Week in\u00a0Apps,\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/this-week-in-apps\/\">the weekly TechCrunch series<\/a>\u00a0that recaps the latest in mobile OS news, mobile applications and the overall app economy.<\/p>\n<p>The app industry is as hot as ever, with\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/app-stores-saw-record-218-billion-downloads-in-2020-consumer-spend-of-143-billion\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a record<\/a>\u00a0218 billion downloads and $143 billion in global consumer spend in 2020.<\/p>\n<p>Consumers last year also\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/app-stores-saw-record-218-billion-downloads-in-2020-consumer-spend-of-143-billion\/\">spent<\/a>\u00a03.5 trillion minutes using apps on Android devices alone. And in the U.S., app usage surged ahead of the time spent watching live TV. Currently, the average American watches 3.7 hours of live TV per day, but now spends four hours per day on their mobile devices.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Apps aren\u2019t just a way to pass idle hours \u2014 they\u2019re also a big business. In 2019, mobile-first companies had a\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/15\/app-stores-saw-record-204-billion-app-downloads-in-2019-consumer-spend-of-120-billion\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">combined<\/a> $544 billion valuation, 6.5x higher than those without a mobile focus. In 2020, investors<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/app-stores-saw-record-218-billion-downloads-in-2020-consumer-spend-of-143-billion\/\"> poured<\/a> $73 billion in capital into mobile companies \u2014 a figure that\u2019s up 27% year-over-year.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"MxtPNpp1r7\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/app-stores-saw-record-218-billion-downloads-in-2020-consumer-spend-of-143-billion\/\">App stores saw record 218 billion downloads in 2020, consumer spend of $143 billion<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;App stores saw record 218 billion downloads in 2020, consumer spend of $143 billion&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/13\/app-stores-saw-record-218-billion-downloads-in-2020-consumer-spend-of-143-billion\/embed\/#?secret=MxtPNpp1r7\" data-secret=\"MxtPNpp1r7\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>This week we&#8217;re looking into the app store bill in Arizona, the trend of animating family photos and what&#8217;s next for Twitter&#8217;s Clubhouse rival, among other things.<\/p>\n<p><strong><em>This Week in Apps will soon be a newsletter! Sign up here:\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/newsletters\">techcrunch.com\/newsletters<\/a>.<\/em><\/strong><\/p>\n<h1>Top Stories<\/h1>\n<h3>Arizona House passes a bill that would allow developers to avoid the &#8220;Apple tax&#8221;<\/h3>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1926417\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1926417\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-1926417\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/gold-apps-.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"554\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/gold-apps-.png 1142w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/gold-apps-.png?resize=150,122 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/gold-apps-.png?resize=300,244 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/gold-apps-.png?resize=768,625 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/gold-apps-.png?resize=680,554 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/gold-apps-.png?resize=50,41 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1926417\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The Arizona House of Representatives this week passed a bill (HB 2005) that could significantly impact Apple and Google&#8217;s grip on the App Store market. Unlike a similar measure recently <a href=\"https:\/\/apnews.com\/article\/technology-north-dakota-fargo-bills-legislation-e69d1f3b2efa1a3740070eddd7e2f1cf\">shot down by the North Dakota Senate,<\/a> this new bill doesn&#8217;t force app stores to offer alternative ways for developers to distribute their apps. Instead, it focuses on giving developers the right to use third-party systems that would allow them to circumvent the 15%-20% cut that Apple and Google take from app sales, in-app purchases and subscriptions.<\/p>\n<p>Apple and Google lobbyists <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/policy\/apple-google-lobbyists-arizona-bill\">were already fighting against this bill<\/a> before it was even formally introduced by Arizona State Rep. Regina Cobb. Cobb says she was approached by a lobbyist representing Match Group and the Coalition for App Fairness (CAF) &#8212; the latter, which has organized some of Apple&#8217;s largest competitors &#8212; like Epic Games, Match Group, Spotify and Tile &#8212; to fight back against Apple&#8217;s control of the app ecosystem.<\/p>\n<p>CAF had also backed <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2021\/02\/14\/technology\/north-dakota-tech-apps.html\">the North Dakota bill,<\/a>, and is helping push legislation in other states, including <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/policy\/apple-google-lobbyists-arizona-bill\">Minnesota, Georgia and Hawaii.<\/a><\/p>\n<p>Some legislators may oppose the bill on the grounds that these decisions are more of a federal matter and concerns over how the state would be able to enforce such a policy. The Arizona bill still has to make it through the Senate (and could be vetoed by Governor Doug Ducey) in order to become a law. If it did pass, it would make Arizona an attractive place to set up an app business and could set the groundwork for other states to pass similar legislation.<\/p>\n<h3>Animated family photos top the App Store<\/h3>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/hashtag\/MyHeritage?src=hash&amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#MyHeritage<\/a> re-animated my grandma Anny (here 16 years old in 1936) and now I&#39;m crying tears of joy, hope, thankfulness, longing &amp; regrets \ud83d\ude0d\ud83d\ude22\ud83d\udc94 <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/uXtjBz2UZV\">pic.twitter.com\/uXtjBz2UZV<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Susanne Wosnitzka \ud83c\udf79 (@Donauschwalbe) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/Donauschwalbe\/status\/1365680787606151170?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">February 27, 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>MyHeritage&#8217;s<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/myheritage-now-lets-you-animate-old-family-photos-using-deepfakery\/\"> recently launched update<\/a> that lets users animate their old photos helped to send the app to the top of the App Store this week. The company had last week introduced &#8220;Deep Nostalgia&#8221; &#8212; a facial animation feature powered by technology from Israeli tech company (and TechCrunch Battlefield alum) D-ID. To animate the photos, the tech maps the facial features from the photo to a driver video to create what it calls a &#8220;live portrait.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The app went viral on social media, including TikTok, as people used the photo to animate long-ago relatives and other historical figures.<\/p>\n<blockquote class=\"tiktok-embed\" style=\"max-width: 605px; min-width: 325px;\" cite=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/@thomasflanigan_\/video\/6935162981919640837\" data-video-id=\"6935162981919640837\">\n<section><a title=\"@thomasflanigan_\" href=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/@thomasflanigan_\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">@thomasflanigan_<\/a>The app is called MyHeritage <a title=\"greenscreenvideo\" href=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/tag\/greenscreenvideo\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">##greenscreenvideo<\/a> <a title=\"myheritage\" href=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/tag\/myheritage\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">##myheritage<\/a> <a title=\"mcdonaldsccsing\" href=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/tag\/mcdonaldsccsing\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">##McDonaldsCCSing<\/a> <a title=\"ancestors\" href=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/tag\/ancestors\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">##ancestors<\/a><a title=\"\u266c record before u listen - penny lane\" href=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/music\/record-before-u-listen-6824616172181408517\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\u266c record before u listen &#8211; penny lane<\/a><\/section>\n<\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/embed.js\"><\/script><\/p>\n<p>But in a number of more touching videos, people film themselves reacting to seeing their mom or dad &#8220;come to life&#8221; again through the tech, blinking, smiling and nodding, often set to &#8220;Remember When&#8221; by Alan Jackson or &#8220;Sign of the Times&#8221; by Harry Styles as the background track.<\/p>\n<p>Though MyHeritage shot up to become the No. 1 Overall app on the App Store as of Tuesday, a smaller startup, Rosebud, quietly pivoted to address the same use case with its <a href=\"https:\/\/www.rosebud.ai\/tokkingheads\">TokkingHeads app<\/a>. The app, founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/www.lishali.com\/\">Berkeley PhD Lisha Li<\/a>, was originally intended for making funny videos and memes with friends, video game avatars or celebs by animating portrait photos with text, speech and puppetry via video &#8212; but not so well that it would cross into &#8220;deepfake&#8221; territory.<\/p>\n<p>But after the release of MyHeritage&#8217;s update, TokkingHeads quickly updated to alert users to its own feature set, while also elevating the MyHeritage-like animations it offers in the app. As a result, the app started to gain a following of its own. On February 28, 2021, TokkingHeads saw 1,000 downloads. The next day, it had 8,000 downloads. The following two days, March 2 and 3, it saw 24,000 downloads and 28,000 downloads, respectively.<\/p>\n<p>The app has since reached as high as No. 12 in the App Store&#8217;s Entertainment category, as of the time of writing, and No. 94 Overall. (And was climbing daily.)<\/p>\n<blockquote class=\"tiktok-embed\" style=\"max-width: 605px; min-width: 325px;\" cite=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/@mirandasevier\/video\/6935646499996994822\" data-video-id=\"6935646499996994822\">\n<section><a title=\"@mirandasevier\" href=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/@mirandasevier\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">@mirandasevier<\/a><a title=\"tokkingheads\" href=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/tag\/tokkingheads\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">#tokkingheads<\/a> <a title=\"fyp\" href=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/tag\/fyp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">#fyp<\/a><a title=\"\u266c Go Rest High On That Mountain - Vince Gill\" href=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/music\/Go-Rest-High-On-That-Mountain-223286290954309632\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\u266c Go Rest High On That Mountain &#8211; Vince Gill<\/a><\/p>\n<\/section>\n<\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/www.tiktok.com\/embed.js\"><\/script><\/p>\n<p>The YC-backed startup&#8217;s ambitions extend beyond animated photos, however. In analysis run on more than 1.3 million Android and iOS apps, researchers found almost 84,000 Android apps and nearly 47,000 iOS apps used public cloud services. Of those, misconfigurations were found in 14% \u2014 11,877 Android apps and 6,608 iOS apps \u2014 which were exposing personal information, passwords and medical information.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Hackers <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/01\/hackers-unc0ver-jailbreak-iphone\/\">released<\/a> a new jailbreak tool for almost every iPhone<\/strong> by using the same vulnerability Apple said last month was under active attack by hackers. Maestro can also be embedded into native mobile apps using a web view.<\/p>\n<p><strong>\ud83e\udd1d Indie weather app <a href=\"https:\/\/weatherlineapp.com\/blog\/weather-line-is-being-acquired\">Weather Line acquired<\/a>.<\/strong> The company didn&#8217;t provide any details on its acquisition, including the buyer, but said the app will be removed from the App Store. Existing users will continue to have access until April 1, 2022.<\/p>\n<p><strong>\ud83d\udcb0 Indian jobs app <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/01\/apple-alum-jobs-app-apna-for-india-workers-raises-12-5-million\/\">Apna<\/a> raised $12.5 million<\/strong> in a round led by Sequoia Capital India and Greenoaks Capital. The app is now used by 80,000 employers and 6 million+ workers such as drivers, delivery personnel, electricians and beauticians.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"AG98AuasAQ\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/01\/apple-alum-jobs-app-apna-for-india-workers-raises-12-5-million\/\">Apple alum\u2019s jobs app for India\u2019s workers raises $12.5 million<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Apple alum\u2019s jobs app for India\u2019s workers raises $12.5 million&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/01\/apple-alum-jobs-app-apna-for-india-workers-raises-12-5-million\/embed\/#?secret=AG98AuasAQ\" data-secret=\"AG98AuasAQ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><strong>\ud83d\udcb0 Istanbul&#8217;s Dream Games <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/28\/istanbuls-dream-games-snaps-up-50m-and-launches-its-first-game-the-puzzle-based-royal-match\/?utm_source=feedburner&amp;utm_medium=feed&amp;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+Techcrunch+%28TechCrunch%29\">raised<\/a> $50 million<\/strong>\u00a0and launched its first mobile gaming title, Royal Match. The round, led by Index Ventures, is the largest Series A raised by a startup in Turkey.<\/p>\n<h1>Downloads<\/h1>\n<p><strong>West Tenth\u00a0<\/strong><\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2119843\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2119843\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2119843\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png 3600w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=2048,1365 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/West-Tenth-9.png?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2119843\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> West Tenth<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/west-tenths-app-encourages-women-to-start-home-businesses-not-join-mlms\/\">West Tenth&#8217;s new app<\/a> aims to give local home-based business owners a platform to reach potential clients and make sales. The <a href=\"https:\/\/www.westtenth.com\/\">app<\/a> focuses on women who have opted out of the traditional workforce to stay home, often to raise kids and work more flexible hours. Often targeted by predatory MLMs, West Tenth aims to convince women that many of their everyday skills are, in fact, marketable businesses &#8212; like cooking and meal prep, party planning, interior design, photography, home organization, baby sleep training, fitness instructions, homemade crafts and more. The startup also offers online education classes to teach women the basics of marketing and running a home business. (iOS and Android)<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"goRmd83Vc3\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/02\/west-tenths-app-encourages-women-to-start-home-businesses-not-join-mlms\/\">West Tenth&#8217;s app encourages women to start home businesses, not join MLMs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; A startup called <a href=\"https:\/\/capp.fm\/\">Cappuccino<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/01\/cappuccino-lets-you-share-short-intimate-audio-stories-with-your-friends\/?utm_source=feedburner&amp;utm_medium=feed&amp;utm_campaign=Feed%3A+Techcrunch+%28TechCrunch%29\">reviewed here by TechCrunch<\/a>, now wants to bring social audio to a more intimate setting: groups of friends. The anti-Clubhouse app lets friends record &#8220;podcasts,&#8221; which are designed for private consumption. (iOS and Android)<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"lStGDbUELp\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/01\/cappuccino-lets-you-share-short-intimate-audio-stories-with-your-friends\/\">Cappuccino lets you share short, intimate audio stories with your friends<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Cappuccino lets you share short, intimate audio stories with your friends&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/01\/cappuccino-lets-you-share-short-intimate-audio-stories-with-your-friends\/embed\/#?secret=lStGDbUELp\" data-secret=\"lStGDbUELp\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<h1>Tweets<\/h1>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">If you had any doubts at all about the Wild Wild West that  are App Store ratings &amp; reviews, someone is currently buying fake 5-star reviews for my own FlickType app &#8211; presumably so that Apple will take my app down.<\/p>\n<p>Apple&#39;s fake review detection is failing *so* miserably. <a href=\"https:\/\/t.co\/kPcCnm7xyM\">pic.twitter.com\/kPcCnm7xyM<\/a><\/p>\n<p>&mdash; Kosta Eleftheriou (@keleftheriou) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/keleftheriou\/status\/1367880602796625925?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 5, 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">In his interview with CNBC and New York Times journalist Andrew Ross Sorkin, Bill Gates said \u201cI actually use an Android phone. Apps","slug":"this-week-in-apps","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576701260"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576701260"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576701260"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576701260"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576701260"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2121945,"date":"2021-03-05T23:58:23","date_gmt":"2021-03-06T07:58:23","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2121945"},"modified":"2021-03-06T08:53:29","modified_gmt":"2021-03-06T16:53:29","slug":"vc-lindy-fishburne-on-the-sudden-democratization-of-science-and-deep-tech-investing","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/vc-lindy-fishburne-on-the-sudden-democratization-of-science-and-deep-tech-investing\/","title":{"rendered":"VC Lindy Fishburne on the seemingly sudden democratization of science"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Deep science investor Lindy Fishburne cofounded the seed- and early-stage venture firm <a href=\"https:\/\/breakout.vc\/\">Breakout Ventures<\/a> several years ago, after cofounding Breakout Labs within the Thiel Foundation back in 2011, and she has amassed a wide array of stakes in the process. Among her firm&#8217;s portfolio companies is <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cortexyme.com\/\">Cortexyme<\/a>, a company that aims to treat Alzheimer&#8217;s disease; the sustainable materials maker <a href=\"https:\/\/www.modernmeadow.com\/\">Modern Meadow<\/a>; and <a href=\"https:\/\/strateos.com\/\">Strateos<\/a>, a company whose robotic cloud platform is remaking how lab work gets done.<\/p>\n<p>We talked with Fishburne late this week about where &#8212; based on what she is seeing &#8212; we are in the arc of this pandemic. We also talked about why more of her investments, which once seemed like long shots, suddenly look like solid bets. Parts of our chat, below, have been edited lightly for length and clarity.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: We want to be excited about the progress being made in vaccinating Americans. Based on the conversations you&#8217;re having, what&#8217;s your sense of things?<\/strong><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>LF: The acceleration of the vaccines is like nothing we&#8217;ve ever seen before in science, and now we really are down to the unsexy part of of the logistics of rolling them out. That&#8217;s clearly our biggest challenge. Then the next piece we&#8217;re going to have to confront is what happens when the world is vaccinated [at] very unequal levels and how people feel about travel and exposure and equity along those issues.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: Science has been the big story of the last year. Are you hearing from investors and potential syndicate partners who weren&#8217;t reaching out previously?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>LF: Yes. The pandemic has brought the importance of investing in science into sharp relief. For the first time, we&#8217;re really seeing a whole set of what you would think of as traditional tech investors who read about the mRNA vaccine that Moderna coded in a weekend and who are starting to believe that we&#8217;re able to engineer biology and that it doesn&#8217;t feel like a craft process anymore.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: You talk about coding a vaccine. Are laboratories becoming less important in that scientists are able to do much more in simulation and, if so, what does that mean for human testing? Are we getting to a point where we don&#8217;t have to rely on human testing as much as we did in the past?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>LF: That&#8217;s where we <em>hope<\/em> to get on the human testing piece. We&#8217;re not there yet. You may have read and heard about organs on a chip and growing organoids, where you can have a very small piece of liver that you&#8217;re able to test toxicity on [and] we&#8217;re doing more of that. That said, we&#8217;re not ready to make that leap from completely doing it in silico to humans with a super-high level of confidence.The human body is such a complex system that we&#8217;re not able to model that fully yet.<\/p>\n<p>I do think what you&#8217;re pointing toward to some degree is democratization in science and the access for more people to be able with lower skills to be able to work in drug discovery and drug development at a distance. So for example, we have a company that we&#8217;ve worked with called Strateos that has a full robotic lab that &#8212; instead of having technicians standing there &#8212; you have robots and a little train track that moves assays throughout the room so that scientists who were stuck at home this year were able to continue experiments regardless of their geography or safety in the lab or time constraints.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: You have another interesting portfolio company, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.opus-12.com\/\">Opus 12<\/a>, which is transforming industrial carbon dioxide emissions into chemicals. Toward what end?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>LF: So obviously, decarbonizing the world is a huge focus. And you&#8217;re seeing for the first time corporations like United Airlines making commitments as to what their carbon footprint will be, or going to zero carbon emissions. Opus 12 emerged from two PhDs and an MBA out of Stanford a few years ago and their breakthrough is a catalyst material that allows you to take for example, waste CO2 &#8212; the bad stuff &#8212; and run it through this catalyst material and produce useful CO. This year, for example, they produced green polycarbonate car parts in partnership with Daimler. The material is exactly the same, which makes it easy to slot into existing products, but it&#8217;s actually made by reusing carbon.<\/p>\n<p>The shift in consumer awareness around carbon made materials is an enormous opportunity.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: Do companies get some sort of carbon credit for doing that?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>LF: Yes, and in the past what we&#8217;ve seen is a lot of companies trying to green themselves by basically buying and trading carbon credits, and the shift that we&#8217;re going through right now is everyone saying, &#8216;Okay, to some degree, that was a bit of financial engineering; now we actually need to see these businesses making a change in their direct use of fossil fuels and their direct impact in the amount of carbon.&#8217; [There&#8217;s growing awareness that] buying carbon offsets isn&#8217;t going to be enough. So you&#8217;re now for the first time really seeing commitments to change processes, supply chain and ultimately products.<\/p>\n<p><strong>TC: In recent years, biotech companies have been going public two and three years after being formed. Now, we&#8217;re seeing a much wider array of younger companies being transformed into public companies through a growing number of blank-check companies. Any thoughts about whether or not there are parallels here?<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>LF: On the therapeutic side, you tend to have a very clear playbook around what the potential exit is and who the acquirers are. We know that big pharma is cash rich and pipeline poor, and so [these pharma giants] have to pick up the assets that are working, and you see them do that regularly. And you&#8217;ve got comps, and you know what that looks like,\u00a0 so in placing a wide range of bets on early-stage therapeutics, it&#8217;s clear that if one wins, you&#8217;re covered.<\/p>\n<p>The SPAC world is going to be really interesting because most of these companies are not operating off traditional playbooks, and it&#8217;s not clear whether they operate as public companies longer term. Are they really set up for acquisition?<\/p>\n<p>[Another] difference here is these companies are going to have this enormous amount of funding, and yet they&#8217;re not going to be able to toil in obscurity, so the traditional metrics that we all want [in] public companies and looking at revenue and profits and those metrics, we&#8217;re going to have to look at these SPACs and their growth through a different lens, and I&#8217;m just not sure how receptive the public markets will be to that in the next 24 months. I think it&#8217;s unclear whether we&#8217;ll have a reckoning there or not.<\/p>\n<p><em>If you&#8217;re curious to learn more, including about why new pots of money might be on the horizon for deep tech startups, you can listen in on our full conversation with Fishburne <a href=\"https:\/\/www.buzzsprout.com\/850276\/8087012\">here<\/a>.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Deep science investor Lindy Fishburne cofounded the seed- and early-stage venture firm Breakout Ventures several years ago, after cofounding Breakout Labs within the Thiel Foundation back in 2011, and she has amassed a wide array of stakes in the process. Among her firm&#8217;s portfolio companies is Cortexyme, a company that aims to treat Alzheimer&#8217;s disease; first look at Coursera\u2019s S-1 filing"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">After TechCrunch broke<\/span> the news yesterday that Coursera was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/04\/coursera-is-planning-to-file-to-go-public-tomorrow\/\">planning to file its S-1<\/a> today, the edtech company officially dropped the document Friday evening.<\/p>\n<p>Coursera was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/07\/21\/edtech-startups-flirt-with-unicorn-style-growth\/\">last valued at $2.4 billion<\/a> by the private markets, when it most recently raised a Series F round in October 2020 that was worth $130 million.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/Archives\/edgar\/data\/1651562\/000119312521071525\/d65490ds1.htm\">Coursera\u2019s S-1 filing<\/a> offers a glimpse into the finances of how an edtech company, accelerated by the pandemic, performed over the past year. It paints a picture of growth, albeit one that came at steep expense.<\/p>\n<h2><strong>Revenue<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>In 2020, Coursera saw $293.5 million in revenue. That\u2019s a roughly 59% increase from the year prior when the company recorded $184.4 million in top line. During that same period, Coursera posted a net loss of nearly $67 million, up 46% from the previous year\u2019s $46.7 million net deficit.<\/p>\n<p>Notably the company had roughly the same noncash, share-based compensation expenses in both years. Even if we allow the company to judge its profitability on an adjusted EBITDA basis, Coursera\u2019s losses still rose from 2019 to 2020, expanding from $26.9 million to $39.8 million.<\/p>\n<p>To understand the difference between net losses and adjusted losses it\u2019s worth unpacking the EBITDA acronym. Standing for &#8220;earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization,&#8221; EBITDA strips out some nonoperating costs to give investors a possible better picture of the continuing health of a business, without getting caught up in accounting nuance. <em>Adjusted<\/em> EBITDA takes the concept one step further, also removing the noncash cost of share-based compensation, and in an even more cheeky move, in this case also deducts \u201cpayroll tax expense related to stock-based activities\u201d as well.<\/p>\n<p>For our purposes, even when we grade Coursera\u2019s profitability on a very polite curve it still winds up generating stiff losses. Indeed, the company\u2019s adjusted EBITDA as a percentage of revenue &#8212; a way of determining profitability in contrast to revenue &#8212; barely improved from a 2019 result of -15% to -14% in 2020.<\/p>\n<p><div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"><\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>After TechCrunch broke the news yesterday that Coursera was planning to file its S-1 today, the edtech company officially dropped the document Friday evening. Coursera was last valued at $2.4 billion by the private markets, when it most recently raised a Series F round in October 2020 that was worth $130 million. Coursera\u2019s S-1 filing California","orientation":"0","keywords":[]},"filesize":1504761},"source_url":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/03\/GettyImages-1008732780.jpeg","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/media\/1961953"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/media"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/types\/attachment"}],"replies":[{"embeddable":true,"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/comments?post=1961953"}],"author":[{"embeddable":true,"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/tc\/v1\/users\/24893112"}]}}]}},{"id":2121874,"date":"2021-03-05T14:29:19","date_gmt":"2021-03-05T22:29:19","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2121874"},"modified":"2021-03-05T19:29:02","modified_gmt":"2021-03-06T03:29:02","slug":"snowflake-latest-enterprise-company-to-feel-wall-streets-wrath-after-good-quarter","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/snowflake-latest-enterprise-company-to-feel-wall-streets-wrath-after-good-quarter\/","title":{"rendered":"Snowflake latest enterprise company to feel Wall Street&#8217;s wrath after good quarter"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Snowflake <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2021\/03\/03\/snowflake-snow-earnings-q4-2021.html\">reported earnings this week<\/a>, and the results look strong with revenue more than doubling year-over-year.<\/p>\n<p>However, while the company&#8217;s fourth quarter revenue rose 117% to $190.5 million, it apparently wasn&#8217;t good enough for investors, who have sent the company&#8217;s stock tumbling since it reported Wednesday after the bell.<\/p>\n<p>It was similar to the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/salesforce-delivers-wall-street-doubts-as-stock-falls-6-3-post-earnings\/\">reaction that Salesforce received<\/a> from Wall Street last week after it announced a positive earnings report. Snowflake&#8217;s stock closed down around 4% today, a recovery compared to its midday lows when it was off nearly 12%.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Why the declines? Wall Street&#8217;s reaction to earnings can lean more on what a company will do next more than its most recent results. But Snowflake&#8217;s guidance for its current quarter appeared strong as well, with a predicted $195 million to $200 million in revenue, numbers in line with analysts&#8217; expectations.<\/p>\n<p>Sounds good, right? Apparently being in line with analyst expectations isn&#8217;t good enough for investors for certain companies. You see, it didn&#8217;t <em>exceed<\/em> the stated expectations, so the results must be bad. I am not sure how meeting expectations is as good as a miss, but there you are.<\/p>\n<p>It&#8217;s worth noting of course that tech stocks have taken a beating so far in 2021. And as my colleague Alex Wilhelm <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/the-technology-selloff-is-getting-to-be-somewhat-material\/\">reported this morning<\/a>, that trend only got worse this week. Consider that the tech-heavy Nasdaq is down 11.4% from its 52-week high, so perhaps investors are flogging everyone and Snowflake is merely caught up in the punishment.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Lr12QvKbHs\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/13\/9-investors-discuss-challenges-opportunities-and-the-impact-of-cloud-vendors-in-enterprise-data-lakes\/\">9 investors discuss hurdles, opportunities and the impact of cloud vendors in enterprise data lakes<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;9 investors discuss hurdles, opportunities and the impact of cloud vendors in enterprise data lakes&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/13\/9-investors-discuss-challenges-opportunities-and-the-impact-of-cloud-vendors-in-enterprise-data-lakes\/embed\/#?secret=Lr12QvKbHs\" data-secret=\"Lr12QvKbHs\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Snowflake CEO Frank Slootman pointed out in the earnings call this week that Snowflake is well positioned, something proven by the fact that his company has removed the data limitations of on-prem infrastructure. The beauty of the cloud is limitless resources, and that forces the company to help customers manage consumption instead of usage, an evolution that works in Snowflake&#8217;s favor.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The big change in paradigm is that historically in on-premise data centers, people have to manage capacity. And now they don\u2019t manage capacity anymore, but they need to manage consumption. And that\u2019s a new thing for &#8212; not for everybody but for most people &#8212; and people that are in the public cloud. I have gotten used to the notion of consumption obviously because it applies equally to the infrastructure clouds,&#8221; Slootman said in the earnings call.<\/p>\n<p>Snowflake has to manage expectations, something that translated into a dozen customers paying $5 million or more on a trailing 12 month basis, according to the company. That&#8217;s a nice chunk of change by any measure. It&#8217;s also clear that while there is a clear tilt toward the cloud, the amount of data that has been moved there is still a small percentage of overall enterprise workloads, meaning there is lots of growth opportunity for Snowflake.<\/p>\n<p>What&#8217;s more, Snowflake executives pointed out that there is a significant ramp up time for customers as they shift data into the Snowflake data lake, but before they push the consumption button. That means that as long as customers continue to move data onto Snowflake&#8217;s platform, they will pay more over time, even if it will take time for new clients to get started.<\/p>\n<p>So why is Snowflake&#8217;s quarterly percentage growth not expanding? Well, as a company gets to the size of Snowflake, it gets harder to maintain those gaudy percentage growth numbers as the law of large numbers begins to kick in.<\/p>\n<p>I&#8217;m not here to tell Wall Street investors how to do their job, anymore than I would expect them to tell me how to do mine. But when you look at the company&#8217;s overall financial picture, the amount of untapped cloud potential and the nature of Snowflake&#8217;s approach to billing, it&#8217;s hard not to be positive about this company&#8217;s outlook, regardless of the reaction of investors in the short term.<\/p>\n<p><em>Note: This article originally stated the company had a dozen customer paying $5 million or more per month. It&#8217;s actually on a trailing 12 month basis and we have updated the article to reflect that.<\/em><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"p3WMatikaO\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/salesforce-delivers-wall-street-doubts-as-stock-falls-6-3-post-earnings\/\">Salesforce delivers, Wall Street doubts as stock falls 6.3% post-earnings<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Salesforce delivers, Wall Street doubts as stock falls 6.3% post-earnings&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/salesforce-delivers-wall-street-doubts-as-stock-falls-6-3-post-earnings\/embed\/#?secret=p3WMatikaO\" data-secret=\"p3WMatikaO\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Snowflake reported earnings this week, and the results look strong with revenue more than doubling year-over-year. owner of Anki&#8217;s assets plans to relaunch Cozmo and Vector this year"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Good robots don\u2019t die &#8212; they just have their assets sold off to the highest bidder. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.digitaldreamlabs.com\/\">Digital Dream Labs<\/a> was there to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.therobotreport.com\/inside-anki-shutdown-who-owns-ip-assets-auction-failed-partnership\/\">sweep up IP<\/a> in the wake of Anki\u2019s premature implosion, back in 2019. The Pittsburgh-based edtech company had initially planned to relaunch Vector and Cozmo at some point in 2020, launching a <a href=\"https:\/\/www.kickstarter.com\/projects\/anki\/vector-by-anki-a-giant-roll-forward-for-robot-kind\/posts\/2724085\">Kickstarter campaign<\/a> in March of last year.<\/p>\n<p>Today, the company<a href=\"https:\/\/www.roboticstomorrow.com\/news\/2021\/03\/05\/cozmo-and-vector-robots-finds-global-retail-distribution-with-protempo\/16415\/\"> announced plans to deliver on the overdue relaunch<\/a>, courtesy of a new distributor.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;There is a tremendous demand for these robots,&#8221; CEO Jacob Hanchar said in a release. &#8220;This partnership will complement the work our teams are already doing to relaunch these products and will ensure that Cozmo and Vector are on shelves for the holidays.&#8221;<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>I don\u2019t doubt that a lot of folks are looking to get their hands on the robots. Cozmo, in particular, was well-received, and sold reasonably well &#8212; but ultimately (and in spite of a lot of funding), the company couldn\u2019t avoid the fate that\u2019s befallen many a robotics startup.<\/p>\n<p>It will be fascinating to see how these machines look when they\u2019re reintroduced. Anki invested tremendous resources into bringing them to life, including the hiring of ex-Pixar and DreamWorks staff to make the robots more lifelike. A lot of thought went into giving the robots a distinct personality, whereas, for instance, Vector\u2019s new owners are making the robot open-source. Cozmo, meanwhile, will have programmable functionality through the company\u2019s app.<\/p>\n<p>It could certainly be an interesting play for the STEM market that companies like Sphero are approaching. It has become a fairly crowded space, but at least Anki\u2019s new owners are building on top of a solid foundation, with the fascinating and emotionally complex toy robots their predecessors created.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Update:<\/strong> We removed a reference to a Kickstarter launched by Anki prior to Digital Dream&#8217;s acquisition of the company&#8217;s IP.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ecISq3dF1B\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/26\/where-these-4-top-vcs-are-investing-in-manufacturing\/\">Where these 4 top VCs are investing in manufacturing<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Where these 4 top VCs are investing in manufacturing&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/26\/where-these-4-top-vcs-are-investing-in-manufacturing\/embed\/#?secret=ecISq3dF1B\" data-secret=\"ecISq3dF1B\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Good robots don\u2019t die &#8212; they just have their assets sold off to the highest bidder. Digital Dream Labs was there to sweep up IP in the wake of Anki\u2019s premature implosion, back in 2019. The Pittsburgh-based edtech company had initially planned to relaunch Vector and Cozmo at some point in 2020, launching a Kickstarter Dream Labs","slug":"digital-dream-labs","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576861280"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576861280"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576861280"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576861280"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576861280"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":2483,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/vector\/","name":"vector","slug":"vector","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/2483"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=2483"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=2483"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=2483"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=2483"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2115572,"date":"2021-03-05T13:31:02","date_gmt":"2021-03-05T21:31:02","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2115572"},"modified":"2021-03-05T10:54:22","modified_gmt":"2021-03-05T18:54:22","slug":"deep-science-ai-adventures-in-arts-and-letters","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/deep-science-ai-adventures-in-arts-and-letters\/","title":{"rendered":"Deep Science: AI adventures in arts and letters"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">There&#8217;s more AI news<\/span> out there than anyone can possibly keep up with. But you can stay tolerably up to date on the most interesting developments with this column, which collects AI and machine learning advancements from around the world and explains why they might be important to tech, startups or civilization.<\/p>\n<p>To begin on a lighthearted note: The ways researchers find to apply machine learning to the arts are always interesting \u2014 though not always practical. A team from the University of Washington wanted to see if a computer vision system could learn to tell what is being played on a piano just from an overhead view of the keys and the player&#8217;s hands.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.washington.edu\/news\/2021\/02\/04\/audeo-teaches-artificial-intelligence-play-piano\/\">Audeo<\/a>, the system trained by Eli Shlizerman, Kun Su and Xiulong Liu, watches video of piano playing and first extracts a piano-roll-like simple sequence of key presses. Then it adds expression in the form of length and strength of the presses, and lastly polishes it up for input into a MIDI synthesizer for output. The results are a little loose but definitely recognizable.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2115580\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/audeo-diagram.png\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2115580\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2115580\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/audeo-diagram.png\" alt=\"Diagram showing how video of a piano player's hands on the keys is turned into MIDI sequences.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"648\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/audeo-diagram.png 2015w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/audeo-diagram.png?resize=150,95 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/audeo-diagram.png?resize=300,190 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/audeo-diagram.png?resize=768,486 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/audeo-diagram.png?resize=680,430 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/audeo-diagram.png?resize=1536,972 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/audeo-diagram.png?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2115580\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Shlizerman, et. al<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;To create music that sounds like it could be played in a musical performance was previously believed to be impossible,&#8221; said Shlizerman. &#8220;An algorithm needs to figure out the cues, or &#8216;features,&#8217; in the video frames that are related to generating music, and it needs to &#8216;imagine&#8217; the sound that\u2019s happening in between the video frames. It requires a system that is both precise and imaginative. The fact that we achieved music that sounded pretty good was a surprise.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Another from the field of arts and letters is this extremely fascinating research into <a href=\"https:\/\/news.mit.edu\/2021\/researchers-virtually-open-sealed-historic-letters-0302\">computational unfolding<\/a> of ancient letters too delicate to handle. The MIT team was looking at &#8220;locked&#8221; letters from the 17th century that are so intricately folded and sealed that to remove the letter and flatten it might permanently damage them. Their approach was to X-ray the letters and set a new, advanced algorithm to work deciphering the resulting imagery.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2121182\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/unfolding-mit.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2121182\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2121182\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/unfolding-mit.jpg\" alt=\"Diagram showing x-ray views of a letter and how it is analyzed to virtually unfold it.\" width=\"1024\" height=\"875\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/unfolding-mit.jpg 1351w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/unfolding-mit.jpg?resize=150,128 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/unfolding-mit.jpg?resize=300,256 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/unfolding-mit.jpg?resize=768,657 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/unfolding-mit.jpg?resize=680,581 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/unfolding-mit.jpg?resize=50,43 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2121182\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Diagram showing X-ray views of a letter and how it is analyzed to virtually unfold it. <strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> MIT<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The algorithm ends up doing an impressive job at separating the layers of paper, despite their extreme thinness and tiny gaps between them, sometimes less than the resolution of the scan,&#8221; MIT&#8217;s Erik Demaine said. &#8220;We weren&#8217;t sure it would be possible.&#8221; The work may be applicable to many kinds of documents that are difficult for simple X-ray techniques to unravel. It&#8217;s a bit of a stretch to categorize this as &#8220;machine learning,&#8221; but it was too interesting not to include. Read the full paper at <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nature.com\/articles\/s41467-021-21326-w\">Nature Communications<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2115581\" style=\"width: 410px\" class=\"wp-caption alignright\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/electric-research.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2115581\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2115581\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/electric-research.jpg\" alt=\"Diagram showing reviews of electric car charge points are analyzed and turned into useful data.\" width=\"400\" height=\"359\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/electric-research.jpg 1440w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/electric-research.jpg?resize=150,135 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/electric-research.jpg?resize=300,269 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/electric-research.jpg?resize=768,689 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/electric-research.jpg?resize=680,610 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/02\/electric-research.jpg?resize=50,45 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 400px) 100vw, 400px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2115581\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Asensio, et. al<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>You arrive at a charge point for your electric car and find it to be out of service. You might even leave a bad review online. In fact, thousands of such reviews exist and constitute a potentially very useful map for municipalities looking to expand electric vehicle infrastructure.<\/p>\n<p>Georgia Tech&#8217;s Omar Asensio <a href=\"https:\/\/www.eurekalert.org\/pub_releases\/2021-01\/cp-att011421.php\">trained a natural language processing model<\/a> on such reviews and it soon became an expert at parsing them by the thousands and squeezing out insights like where outages were common, comparative cost and other factors.<div
