class=\"more-articles-title\">More posts by this contributor<\/span>\n\t\t<ul class=\"more-articles-list\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/09\/meet-the-entrepreneurs-bringing-bitcoin-to-institutions\/\">Meet the entrepreneurs bringing bitcoin to institutions<\/a><\/li>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<li><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/24\/how-emerging-markets-are-approaching-crypto\/\">How emerging markets are approaching crypto<\/a><\/li>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/ul>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/div>\n<\/div><p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It\u2019s hard to imagine a worse scenario than the one left behind by former Treasury Secretary Steven Mnuchin.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/08\/bitcoin-advocates-revolt-against-the-trump-administrations-frantic-crypto-regulations\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">draconian regulatory proposals<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> were Mnuchin\u2019s own personal vendetta, according to Bitcoin veterans like<\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.vice.com\/en\/article\/k7anmv\/the-era-of-government-friendly-bitcoin-miners-is-here\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Square Crypto developer Matt Corallo<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coincenter.org\/people\/jerry-brito\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Coin Center <\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">director Jerry Brito, and it\u2019s too soon to say whether incoming Treasury Secretary Janet Yellen will approve the proposed know-your-customer standards or reject them.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Given the chaos created by the Trump administration, bitcoin fans are anxiously optimistic about how regulators will approach the cryptocurrency space during President Joe Biden\u2019s administration.\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mnuchin at the very end had an alarmist view about the illicit use of cryptocurrency that wasn\u2019t shared by law enforcement and intelligence agencies. It doesn\u2019t seem that Janet Yellen has that same view,\u201d Brito said. \u201cHer view seems to be very standard.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Namely, Yellen believes there are both <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/janet-yellen-offers-senate-a-more-nuanced-take-on-crypto\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">positive <\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">and <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/crypto-use-in-terrorism-a-growing-problem-yellen-says\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">negative ways <\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">to use cryptocurrency. She\u2019s expressed a desire to strengthen regulations that prevent illicit usage like terror financing. She may set the tone for government bodies like the Office of the Comptroller of the Currency (OCC), the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) and the Commodity Futures Trading Commission (CFTC).\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"gxjKmsUL0R\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/08\/bitcoin-advocates-revolt-against-the-trump-administrations-frantic-crypto-regulations\/\">Bitcoin advocates revolt against the Trump administration&#8217;s frantic crypto regulations<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Bitcoin advocates revolt against the Trump administration&#8217;s frantic crypto regulations&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/08\/bitcoin-advocates-revolt-against-the-trump-administrations-frantic-crypto-regulations\/embed\/#?secret=gxjKmsUL0R\" data-secret=\"gxjKmsUL0R\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe SEC, OCC and CFTC are choosing people that are very crypto knowledgeable,\u201d Brito added. \u201cThat could tell you they are getting deep knowledge to regulate it heavily or, more likely, it\u2019s now seen as an important part of the economy and finance.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Although it\u2019s still early in the transition, it appears the Biden administration will nominate former Ripple advisor and former U.S. Treasury Department official <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/former-ripple-board-member-tapped-to-lead-bidens-occ-wsj\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Michael Barr<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> to head the OCC. In the short term, Trump\u2019s SEC appointee, <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/jasonbrett\/2020\/08\/06\/us-senate-votes-in-crypto-mom-hester-peirce-at-sec-through-2025\/?sh=5e4348561524\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Commissioner Hester Pierce<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, will continue her notoriously crypto-friendly approach to the securities market. But the Biden administration is reportedly considering former <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/crypto-gary-gensler-sec-tea-leaves\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">CFTC chairman Gary Gensler<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> to soon lead the SEC.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;The new SEC Chairman Gary Gensler has been pretty outspoken with his views on Facebook\u2019s project Libra, as well as Ripple. It\u2019s his opinion that those are securities and should be regulated by the SEC,&#8221; said attorney Hailey Lennon, a crypto-focused partner at <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.andersonkill.com\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Anderson Kill law firm<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. \u201cIn the next year or two, I hope some of the litigation we are seeing and new leadership in the SEC, will result in greater clarity so that down the road there are less enforcement actions. Clarity will help companies to know what to avoid.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Meanwhile, Reuters reported the White House is expected to nominate <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/article\/usa-biden-cftc-idUSL4N2JW3W5\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Georgetown University professor Chris Brummer<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> to lead the CFTC. Brummer was previously <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/chris-brummer-to-be-bidens-cftc-chair-crypto-friendly-tarbert-steps-down\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">President Obama\u2019s pick<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, but never got confirmed by the Senate due to political gridlocks. It\u2019s still unclear who will be <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/trump-presidency-crypto-legacy\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">nominated in 2021 for key roles <\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">related to curbing terror financing, such as the <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Office of Foreign Assets Control (OFAC) and the Financial Crimes Enforcement Network (FinCEN).\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;I think we might start seeing more regulation coming from FinCEN and OFAC. There have been some settlements with crypto companies and OFAC has been adding wallet addresses to the SDN [sanctions] list,\u201d Lennon said. \u201cEven if we see more positive things coming from the OCC, SEC and CFTC, it will be balanced a bit with more regulations related to know-your-customer and anti-money laundering, more general supervision of the source of funds and sanctions screening.&#8221;<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Sanctions are the hot topic of 2021. Throughout 2020, the<\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/iran-concerns-may-be-driving-trump-administrations-talk-of-new-crypto-rules\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Iranian government<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> published statements indicating it intends to use cryptocurrency, including <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/rouhani-bitcoin-mining-iran\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">bitcoin<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> but not limited to it, to <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/iranian-general-advocates-crypto-use-for-skirting-sanctions-report\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">circumnavigate banking sanctions<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.\u00a0<\/span>Emigres from Iran and other countries <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/21\/how-bitcoin-is-helping-middle-class-users-survive-the-pandemic\/\">have used bitcoin to do exactly this<\/a>.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"FgW1BSX4oF\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/03\/11\/bitcoin-gets-slower-smaller-and-more-like-ethereum\/\">Bitcoin gets slower, smaller and more like Ethereum<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Bitcoin gets slower, smaller and more like Ethereum&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/03\/11\/bitcoin-gets-slower-smaller-and-more-like-ethereum\/embed\/#?secret=FgW1BSX4oF\" data-secret=\"FgW1BSX4oF\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">So far, the <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.timesofisrael.com\/biden-faces-imminent-decision-time-on-future-of-iran-nuclear-deal\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Biden administration<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> hasn\u2019t offered any indication it might <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.theguardian.com\/world\/2021\/jan\/28\/iran-disappointed-after-biden-administration-says-sanctions-to-stay-in-place\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">lift sanctions<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. To the contrary, on February 18, the <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/home.treasury.gov\/policy-issues\/financial-sanctions\/recent-actions\/20210218\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Treasury published a statement<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> that the payment processor BitPay was penalized for allowing users to transact with citizens in sanctions jurisdictions like Iran, Cuba and Ukraine. Regulators&#8217; approach to cryptocurrency, which many Iranian-Americans also use both internationally and domestically, will reflect whether the White House prefers a hawkish or dovish approach to diplomacy in the Middle East.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Perianne Boring, founder of an advocacy group called the <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/digitalchamber.org\/?source=em\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Chamber of Digital Commerce<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, said \u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">the new administration and leadership have signaled a critical perspective\u201d of the broader cryptocurrency space. As such, Boring said she hopes industry leaders will continue to engage with lawmakers to \u201clay the foundation for America\u2019s leadership role\u201d in global crypto markets.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">She said American crypto startups are competing in global arenas, against startups based in<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> nations with more progressive laws as nations strive to foster the \u201cnext Silicon Valley.\u201d <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/currency-cold-war-takes-center-stage-at-pre-davos-crypto-confab\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Other nations<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> are encouraging crypto companies, especially domestic <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/how-bitcoins-price-slump-is-changing-the-geography-of-mining\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">crypto mining<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> industries. Many technologists believe it behooves American leaders to defend dollar dominance by cultivating innovation in this tech sector. After all, many of the leading <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/defipulse.com\/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">stablecoins <\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">are still <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/why-tether-volume-surged-to-all-time-highs-in-august\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">denominated<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> in American dollars.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe Biden-Harris administration and Congress must make clear that addressing digital asset and blockchain policies are a priority,\u201d Boring said. \u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Biden-Harris administration should be focused now on growing the economy back to full employment and robust quarterly and annual economic growth.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"oFLtjB9A7z\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/21\/how-bitcoin-is-helping-middle-class-users-survive-the-pandemic\/\">How Bitcoin is helping middle-class users survive the pandemic<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;How Bitcoin is helping middle-class users survive the pandemic&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/21\/how-bitcoin-is-helping-middle-class-users-survive-the-pandemic\/embed\/#?secret=oFLtjB9A7z\" data-secret=\"oFLtjB9A7z\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Brito said he\u2019s especially curious to see new appointees for OFAC and FinCEN, since they\u2019ll be Yellen\u2019s right and left hand in her approach to sanctions and regulations. He agreed with Lennon and Boring, all of whom believe new legal norms are in the pipeline. However stringent, or pro-business, the coming verdicts may be, at least Biden has yet to <\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/what-trumps-bitcoin-tweet-changes\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">rage tweet<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> about hating bitcoin, the way Trump did.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIt\u2019s still that period where everyone is getting their sea legs and trying to understand what their priorities are,\u201d Brito said of the Biden administration. \u201cOnce they start either putting forth policy or reacting to the things that happen, that\u2019s when we\u2019ll really know where they stand.\u201d\u00a0 <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: Biden","slug":"joe-biden","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/143640"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=143640"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=143640"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=143640"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=143640"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2121850,"date":"2021-03-05T12:58:23","date_gmt":"2021-03-05T20:58:23","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2121850"},"modified":"2021-03-05T13:43:40","modified_gmt":"2021-03-05T21:43:40","slug":"tesla-has-closed-its-forums-to-launch-a-social-platform-and-fans-are-not-happy","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/tesla-has-closed-its-forums-to-launch-a-social-platform-and-fans-are-not-happy\/","title":{"rendered":"Tesla has closed its forums to launch a social platform and fans are not happy"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Tesla plans to shut down the forums section on its website as it launches a new social platform called the Tesla Engagement Platform, a move that&#8217;s raised the ire of a community of its most ardent supporters.<\/p>\n<p>Tesla first announced the new engagement platform with a notice at the top of its forums page that reads: &#8220;Starting March 15th, Tesla Forums will become read only. To continue the conversation with the Tesla community visit engage.tesla.com.&#8221; The Verge was the<a href=\"https:\/\/www.theverge.com\/2021\/3\/5\/22315339\/tesla-social-platform-cleaner-energy-forums-charity\"> first to report the changes<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Rather than create posts and threads, the new site invites owners and fans of the brand to engage by commenting on Tesla&#8217;s public-policy-related posts and campaigns that run the gamut, including calls to support the company&#8217;s disaster relief efforts in Texas and requests for Nebraskans to ask their state lawmakers to encourage the passing of a bill that would allow the direct sale of Teslas in certain districts.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>In the replies of a <a href=\"https:\/\/forums.tesla.com\/discussion\/183426\/end-of-tesla-forums\">March 2 Tesla forum post<\/a> announcing the 13-day countdown until the platform&#8217;s demise, one commenter with supposed &#8220;inside info&#8221; alleged that the forums were closing because Tesla couldn&#8217;t afford to hire multiple full-time moderators to keep up with the barrage of spam and trolls that would frequent the threads.<\/p>\n<p>Those trolls are likely to migrate to Twitter now, as the Tesla Engagement Platform will be moderated.<\/p>\n<p>The forums, which will now be available as read-only archives, were a place for Tesla fans, investors and verified owners to ask and answer each other&#8217;s questions. However, the unmoderated nature of the forum led to an environment where its most active posters would, at times, attack people for raising concerns. The new microsite, which also helps people apply for membership to local owners&#8217; clubs, promises a direct feedback loop with the company&#8217;s policy team and encourages visitors to get involved in Tesla advocacy.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Engage Tesla is a new platform for both Tesla&#8217;s public policy team and Tesla Owner&#8217;s Clubs,&#8221; reads the <a href=\"https:\/\/engage.tesla.com\/articles\/14-welcome-tesla-engagement-platform\">first post on the new microsite<\/a>. &#8220;Its goal is to create a digital home base for all of our work, and make it easier for Tesla community members to learn what&#8217;s top of mind for us, take meaningful action, and stay in the loop. We hope you&#8217;ll join us in getting involved.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>A quick skim through the comments section of the first post reveals a bevy of unhappy users who want the forums to stay, or at least remade into something similar &#8212; and moderated &#8212; on the new site. There are no shortage of Tesla and other EV-related forums on the internet. This one has been held up as a bastion of toxicity, while being lauded as a place for owners and potential buyers to share honest information on the good and bad parts of the company&#8217;s products.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Please do not get rid of the Forums,&#8221; implored one commenter. &#8220;This is not a replacement. The forums (with exception of the trolls on it) brought about informed discussion to help fellow owners with issues.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Indeed, the new platform doesn&#8217;t appear to be a replacement. It looks more like a blog that shares industry news, Tesla events and campaigns, an effort to gather the work already being done by its supporters in one place and encourage further advocacy on the company&#8217;s behalf. For example, the Tesla Owners club in Silicon Valley had already raised $10,000 to support the Del Valle, Texas community, which surrounds the area in which the company&#8217;s new factory is being built.<\/p>\n<p>Not everyone is a critic. While many of the initial comments on the platform&#8217;s first post call for a moderated forum, some suggest improvements to the company&#8217;s customer service department and others request resources on how to advocate for public charging infrastructure. It&#8217;s still early days for the new engagement platform. We&#8217;ll see how engaging Tesla&#8217;s fans truly find it to be.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"8bdEWLhSXh\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/24\/can-solid-state-batteries-power-up-for-the-next-generation-of-evs\/\">Can solid state batteries power up for the next generation of EVs?<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Can solid state batteries power up for the next generation of EVs?&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/24\/can-solid-state-batteries-power-up-for-the-next-generation-of-evs\/embed\/#?secret=8bdEWLhSXh\" data-secret=\"8bdEWLhSXh\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Tesla plans to shut down the forums section on its website as it launches a new social platform called the Tesla Engagement Platform, a move that&#8217;s raised the ire of a community of its most ardent supporters. {"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?categories=17396"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?categories=17396"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?categories=17396"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[{"id":197443,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/electric-vehicles\/","name":"electric vehicles","slug":"electric-vehicles","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/197443"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=197443"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=197443"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=197443"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=197443"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":429989,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/tesla\/","name":"Tesla","slug":"tesla","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/429989"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=429989"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=429989"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=429989"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=429989"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2121706,"date":"2021-03-05T12:08:31","date_gmt":"2021-03-05T20:08:31","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2121706"},"modified":"2021-03-05T17:01:57","modified_gmt":"2021-03-06T01:01:57","slug":"california-bill-would-require-all-self-driving-vehicles-to-be-zero-emission-by-2025","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/california-bill-would-require-all-self-driving-vehicles-to-be-zero-emission-by-2025\/","title":{"rendered":"California bill would require all self-driving vehicles to be zero emission by 2025"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">California might be the first state to give self-driving cars a deadline to electrify.<\/p>\n<p>In mid-February, a bill was quietly introduced into the California State Legislature that would require all autonomous vehicles to also be zero emission by 2025. Proposed <a href=\"https:\/\/leginfo.legislature.ca.gov\/faces\/billTextClient.xhtml?bill_id=202120220SB500\">Bill SB 500<\/a>, which was introduced by Senator Dave Min and sponsored by the Union of Concerned Scientists (UCS), would directly affect the nascent AV industry in applications like ride-hailing, delivery and trucking.<\/p>\n<p>The amendment is in line with many of California&#8217;s goals to reduce emissions. It would add to the state&#8217;s vehicle code, which currently provides for programs to promote zero-emission vehicles, such as the Clean Vehicle Rebate Project and the Charge Ahead California Initiative.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Governor Gavin Newsom has said he wants all new vehicle sales to be zero emission by 2035, but that doesn&#8217;t apply to commercial fleets. Not unless this bill is passed. The proposed bill is in its infancy stages, so there are plenty of opportunities for it to be quashed. But it surfaces an issue for a burgeoning AV industry and the companies trying to develop and commercialize autonomous driving technology in California. It also has the potential to provide a boost to the companies that only use electric vehicles.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;California has set important standards to aggressively address our climate crisis,&#8221; Min told TechCrunch. &#8220;My SB 500 aligns with these ambitions and takes a critical first step in requiring autonomous vehicles to be zero emission before they are put to widespread use.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Proponents of the bill don&#8217;t want to see future means of transportation married to the technology of the past, pointing out the potential for AVs to either help or hurt attempts to cut emissions. California has a reputation for leading the rest of the country in EV adoption and other emissions-related policies, so the success or failure of this bill could create ripple effects in states across the nation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;It definitely seems like we&#8217;re going to start seeing AVs in these fleet applications, whether that&#8217;s ride-hailing or delivery, and that makes it even more important that these vehicles are electric,&#8221; said Elizabeth Irvin, senior transportation analyst at UCS. &#8220;The average person drives their car 11,000 to 13,000 miles per year, but a full-time Uber or Lyft driver drives 30,000 or more.&#8221;<\/p>\n<h2>The strategy<\/h2>\n<p>Close to half of California&#8217;s greenhouse gas emissions come from transportation. And while there&#8217;s nothing quite like a smoggy Los Angeles sunset, supporters say the danger of not placing requirements on the AV industry could lead to a world in which autonomous commercial vehicles are commonplace and powered by fossil fuels.<\/p>\n<p>In a statement defending support of this bill, UCS points to research that shows how AVs could dramatically increase driving, and thus emissions, as people get used to living the luxurious life of a passenger.<a href=\"https:\/\/ucsusa.org\/sites\/default\/files\/attach\/2019\/02\/Where-Are-Self-Driving-Cars-Taking-Us-web.pdf\"> One study<\/a>, which examined the potential effects of AVs on the Washington, D.C. metropolitan region transportation system in 2040, found that AVs would cause the total amount of driving to increase by as much as 66% relative to the 2040 baseline year.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ytX9CqIjWZ\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/02\/27\/californias-self-driving-car-reports-are-public-heres-what-they-dont-mean\/\">California&#8217;s self-driving car reports are public. Here&#8217;s what they don&#8217;t mean.<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;California&#8217;s self-driving car reports are public. Here&#8217;s what they don&#8217;t mean.&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/02\/27\/californias-self-driving-car-reports-are-public-heres-what-they-dont-mean\/embed\/#?secret=ytX9CqIjWZ\" data-secret=\"ytX9CqIjWZ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Irvin told TechCrunch that UCS has been in talks with various stakeholders &#8212; such as Nuro, the SoftBank-backed autonomous delivery startup, and Cruise, General Motor&#8217;s self-driving subsidiary &#8212; regarding strategies for advancing policy that would require all AVs to be zero-emission in California before mainstream adoption.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are supportive of efforts to accelerate the industry&#8217;s transition to clean energy, which aligns with Nuro&#8217;s goals and values,&#8221; said a spokesperson from Nuro. &#8220;We are excited for autonomous vehicles to pave the way for the rest of the auto industry, which we believe will lead to a greener and healthier future.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2121834\" style=\"width: 2107px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/nuro-lineup.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2121834\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2121834 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/nuro-lineup.jpg\" alt=\"nuro av lineup\" width=\"2097\" height=\"927\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/nuro-lineup.jpg 2097w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/nuro-lineup.jpg?resize=150,66 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/nuro-lineup.jpg?resize=300,133 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/nuro-lineup.jpg?resize=768,340 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/nuro-lineup.jpg?resize=680,301 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/nuro-lineup.jpg?resize=1536,679 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/nuro-lineup.jpg?resize=2048,905 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2021\/03\/nuro-lineup.jpg?resize=50,22 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2097px) 100vw, 2097px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2121834\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Nuro<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The sentiment is mirrored by Cruise, which unveiled last year a <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/21\/cruise-unveils-origin-an-electric-driverless-vehicle-designed-for-sharing\/\">driverless vehicle called Origin<\/a> that&#8217;s designed for sharing and powered by an all-electric platform built by GM, the result of a multi-year partnership with Honda. Cruise is not testing autonomous Origin vehicles in San Francisco yet; the battery platform is still undergoing testing at GM&#8217;s proving grounds. Cruise does have aspirations to roll out a fleet of autonomous vehicles \u2014 initially using the all-electric Chevrolet Bolt \u2014 as part of a ride-hailing, and possibly a delivery, service in San Francisco.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"4Xx2OVeZSd\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/21\/cruise-unveils-origin-an-electric-driverless-vehicle-designed-for-sharing\/\">Cruise unveils Origin, an electric driverless vehicle designed for sharing<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Cruise unveils Origin, an electric driverless vehicle designed for sharing&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/01\/21\/cruise-unveils-origin-an-electric-driverless-vehicle-designed-for-sharing\/embed\/#?secret=4Xx2OVeZSd\" data-secret=\"4Xx2OVeZSd\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;Because this industry is so new, everyone has a choice to be an EV or not,&#8221; Rob Grant, <span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">SVP government affairs at Cruise, <\/span><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">told TechCrunch. &#8220;It&#8217;s not like you have to transform an existing fleet. You have a choice to do this in the beginning rather than going down this path and being forced to change it at some later date.&#8221;<\/span><\/p>\n<h2>Hybrids versus electric<\/h2>\n<p>Not all AVs use electric vehicles. The Ford Fusion hybrid and Chrysler Pacifica Plug-in Hybrid minivans have been the go-to choices for AV developers, including Argo AI, Aurora, Waymo and Voyage.<\/p>\n<p>Argo AI is a technology platform company that works with major automakers, like Volkswagen and Ford, to develop autonomous driving systems. While Volkswagen&#8217;s ID.Buzz will be the company&#8217;s first fully electric self-driving car, Ford still prefers to take a more measured approach by modifying the hybrid Ford Fusion.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We all want to transition to BEVs eventually, but we also need to find the right balance that will help develop a profitable, viable business model,&#8221; John Davis, chief engineer at Ford Autonomous Vehicles said. &#8220;This means launching with hybrids first.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Davis outlined various challenges in developing all-electric vehicles as AVs, including depletion of range from on-board tech, decreased use of the vehicle during charge times and degradation of the battery.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Testing shows that upwards of 50% of BEV range will be used up due to the computing power of an AV system, plus the A\/C and entertainment systems that are likely required during a ride-hailing service (for passenger comfort),&#8221; Davis said. &#8220;We continue to be encouraged as battery chemistry and cost continue to improve to address these issues.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1907217\" style=\"width: 3630px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/GettyImages-1142125645.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1907217\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-1907217 size-full\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/GettyImages-1142125645.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"3620\" height=\"2343\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/GettyImages-1142125645.jpg 3620w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/GettyImages-1142125645.jpg?resize=150,97 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/GettyImages-1142125645.jpg?resize=300,194 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/GettyImages-1142125645.jpg?resize=768,497 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/GettyImages-1142125645.jpg?resize=680,440 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/GettyImages-1142125645.jpg?resize=1536,994 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/GettyImages-1142125645.jpg?resize=2048,1326 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/11\/GettyImages-1142125645.jpg?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 3620px) 100vw, 3620px\" \/><\/a><p id=\"caption-attachment-1907217\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image credits<\/strong>: Andrej Sokolow\/dpa picture alliance via Getty Images<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Waymo tested and then launched a robotaxi service in a limited and growing area in the Phoenix suburbs. And while the company has never officially announced it will launch a commercial service in California, its activities over the years all point to that intention. The Mountain View, California-based company regularly tests its vehicles, which includes the electric Jaguar I-Pace, in San Francisco and the surrounding area. The company said it supports Newsom&#8217;s recent executive order, but stopped short of endorsing the current language in Min&#8217;s bill.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;As the first company to commercially deploy our fully autonomous technology to the public, we strongly support the goals outlined in Governor Newsom&#8217;s recent Executive Order N-79-20 which takes a holistic approach to transition California towards a 100% EV future,&#8221; a Waymo spokesperson told TechCrunch. &#8220;Waymo has business lines and partnerships that span ride-hailing, trucking and local delivery, and we want to ensure that California&#8217;s EV policy reflects the myriad issues and industries affected. It&#8217;s early in the legislative process, and we look forward to working with Sen. Min in his efforts.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Industry sources familiar with the bill have noted that the current language, which is fairly brief, is just a placeholder and unlikely to make much headway this session. Those same sources have criticized the sponsors and author for neglecting to specify a plan for charging infrastructure or making distinctions between light and heavy-duty vehicles. Trucks carrying freight are expected to be among the first vehicles with widespread autonomous use. Most self-driving truck development occurs outside of California in regulatory-light states like Arizona and Texas. And while there are some efforts to develop electric and autonomous semi trucks, most testing today involves diesel-powered vehicles. That could prompt companies hoping to deploy in California to lean on the senator&#8217;s office to include an exemption for heavy-duty vehicles.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;re still looking to fill out details as we move through the legislative process, but UCS&#8217;s intention is that this bill stay focused on the electrification requirement,&#8221; responded Irvin.<\/p>\n<hr \/>\n<p><em><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/02\/26\/techcrunch-early-stage-is-the-startup-bootcamp-youve-always-needed\/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">Early Stage<\/a> is the premier \u2018how-to\u2019 event for startup entrepreneurs and investors. You\u2019ll hear first-hand how some of the most successful founders and VCs build their businesses, raise money and manage their portfolios. We\u2019ll cover every aspect of company-building: Fundraising, recruiting, sales, product market fit, PR, marketing and brand building. Each session also has audience participation built-in \u2013 there\u2019s ample time included for audience questions and vehicles","slug":"self-driving-vehicles","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449550916"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449550916"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449550916"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449550916"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449550916"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":449556932,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/waymo\/","name":"waymo","slug":"waymo","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449556932"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449556932"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449556932"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449556932"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449556932"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2083654,"date":"2021-03-05T11:30:19","date_gmt":"2021-03-05T19:30:19","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2083654"},"modified":"2021-03-04T15:14:47","modified_gmt":"2021-03-04T23:14:47","slug":"product-manager-hiring-for-startups","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/05\/product-manager-hiring-for-startups\/","title":{"rendered":"How and when to hire your first product manager"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">In the world<\/span> of early-stage startups, job titles are often a formality. In reality, each employee may handle a dozen responsibilities outside their job description. The choose-your-own-adventure type of work style is part of the magic of startups and often why generalists thrive here.<\/p>\n<p>However, as a company progresses and the team grows, there comes a time when a founder needs to carve out dedicated roles. Of these positions, product management might be one of the most elusive \u2014 and key \u2014 roles to fill.<\/p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--right\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\tProduct management might be one of the most elusive \u2014 and key \u2014 roles to fill.\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/p>\n<p>We spoke to startup founders and operators to get their thoughts about how and when they hired their first product manager. Some of the things we talked about were:<\/p>\n<ul>\n<li>\u00a0Which traits to look for.<\/li>\n<li>\u00a0Why it&#8217;s important to define the role before you look for your best fit.<\/li>\n<li>\u00a0Whether your new hire needs to have a technical background.<\/li>\n<li>\u00a0The best questions to ask in an interview.<\/li>\n<li>\u00a0How to time your first hire and avoid overhiring.<\/li>\n<\/ul>\n<h2><strong>Don\u2019t hire for the CEO of a product<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>Let\u2019s start by working backward. Product managers often graduate into a CEO role or leave a company to become a founder. Like founders, talented product managers have innate leadership skills and are able to effectively and clearly communicate. Similarly, both roles require a person who is a visionary when it comes to the product and execution.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/davidblake?ref_src=twsrc%5Egoogle%7Ctwcamp%5Eserp%7Ctwgr%5Eauthor\">David Blake<\/a> was a product manager before he became a serial edtech founder who created <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/06\/16\/degreed-lands-new-cash-for-upskilling-in-a-down-market\/\">Degreed<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/16\/learn-in-thinks-a-solution-to-layoffs-is-more-sabbaticals\/\">Learn In<\/a>, and most recently,<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/24\/the-first-rule-of-bookclub-no-boring-book-clubs\/\"> BookClub<\/a>. He says that experience helped him launch the first prototype of Degreed and attract first clients.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThe must-have skill is the ability to put the team&#8217;s best wisdom in check and inform the product decisions with users and potential clients to inform what you are building,\u201d he said. The person \u201cmust also be able to take the team&#8217;s mission and develop and sell that narrative to users and potential clients. That is how you blaze a new trail, balance risk, while avoiding building a &#8216;faster horse.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The overlapping synergies between PMs and founders is part of the reason why the role is so confusing to define and hire for. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.kennorton.com\/about\/\">Ken Norton,<\/a> former director of product at Figma who recently left to solo advise and coach product managers, says companies can start by defining what PMs are not: The CEO of the product.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIt\u2019s about not handing off the product responsibilities to somebody,\u201d he said. \u201cYou want the founder and the CEO to continue to be the evangelist and visionary.\u201d Instead, the role is more about day to day \u201cblocking and tackling.&#8221; Norton wrote a piece more than 15 years ago about <a href=\"https:\/\/www.kennorton.com\/essays\/productmanager.html\">how to hire a product manager<\/a>, and it&#8217;s still an essential read for anyone interested in the field.<\/p>\n<h2><strong>Define the role and set your expectations <\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>Product managers help translate all the jugglers within a startup to each other; connecting the engineer with marketing, design with business development and sales with all the above. The role at its core is hard to define, but at the same time is the necessary plumbing for any startup that wants to be high-growth and ambitious.<\/p>\n<p>While a successful product manager is a strong generalist, they have to have the ability to understand and humanize technical processes. The best candidates, then, have some sort of technical experience as an engineer or otherwise.<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"><\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>In the world of early-stage startups, job titles are often a formality. The choose-your-own-adventure type of work style is part of the magic of startups and often why generalists thrive here. However, as a company progresses and the team grows, there comes
